adaIds;\n403\t}\n404\t\n405\t/**\n406\t * Infer borough from station name or coordinates.\n407\t *\n408\t * Strategy: check name first for unambiguous cases, then use coordinates\n409\t * as a The coordinate boundaries are approximate.\n410\t *\n411\t * Note: some stations (e.g., complex stations like 125 St) have parts in\n412\t * multiple boroughs. ||\n601\t    n.includes(\"soho\") ||\n602\t    n.includes(\"greenwich\") ||\n603\t    n.includes(\"tribeca\") ||\n604\t    n.includes(\"chinatown\") ||\n605\t    n.includes(\"lower east\") ||\n606\t }\n635\t\n636\t  // Queens: east of Manhattan (less negative longitude)\n637\t  // Extended to -73.93 to capture Queens Blvd corridor stations\n638\t  if (lon > -73.93 && lat > 40.55 && lat < 40.78) Default to Manhattan for central NYC\n648\t  return \"manhattan\";\n649\t}\n650\t\n651\t/**\n652\t * Process stops.txt into stations.json\n653\t */\n654\tfunction processStops(stopsData, tripsData, stopTimesData) {\n655\t  log(\"Processing stops...\");\n656\t\n657\t  // Build trip_id -> route_id mapping\n658\t  const tripToRoute = new Map();\n659\t  for (const trip of tripsData) {\n660\t    tripToRoute.set(trip.trip_id, trip.route_id);\n661\t  }\n662\t\n663\t  // Build stop_id -> set of route_ids\n664\t  const stopToRoutes = new Map();\n665\t  for (const st of stopTimesData) {\n666\t    const routeId = tripToRoute.get(st.trip_id);\n667\t    if (routeId) {\n668\t      if (!stopToRoutes.has(st.stop_id)) {\n669\t        stopToRoutes.set(st.stop_id, new Set());\n670\t      }\n671\t      stopToRoutes.get(st.stop_id).add(routeId);\n672\t    }\n673\t  }\n674\t\n675\t  // Separate parent stations from child stops\n676\t  const parentStations = [];\n677\t  const childStops = new Map();\n678\t\n679\t  for (const stop of stopsData) {\n680\t    const locationType = parseInt(stop.location_type || \"0\", 10);\n681\t    if (locationType === 1) {\n682\t      parentStations.push(stop);\n683\t    } else {\n684\t      childStops.set(stop.stop_id, stop);\n685\t    }\n686\t  }\n687\t\n688\t  // Build stations index\n689\t  const stations = {};\n690\t\n691\t  for (const parent of parentStations) {\n692\t    const stationId = parent.stop_id;\n693\t    const name = parent.stop_name;\n694\t    const lat = parseFloat(parent.stop_lat);\n695\t    const lon = parseFloat(parent.stop_lon);\n696\t\n697\t    let northStopId = null;\n698\t    let southStopId = null;\n699\t    const allLines = new Set();\n700\t\n701\t    for (const [childId, child] of childStops) {\n702\t      if (child.parent_station === stationId) {\n703\t        if (childId.endsWith(\"N\")) {\n704\t          northStopId = childId;\n705\t        } else if (childId.endsWith(\"S\")) {\n706\t          southStopId = childId;\n707\t        }\n708\t\n709\t        const routes = stopToRoutes.get(childId) || new Set();\n710\t        for (const r of routes) {\n711\t          if (!EXCLUDED_LINE_VARIANTS.has(r)) {\n712\t            allLines.add(r);\n713\t          }\n714\t        }\n715\t      }\n716\t    }\n717\t\n718\t    // Also collect routes from parent station itself\n719\t    const parentRoutes = stopToRoutes.get(stationId) || new Set();\n720\t    for (const r of parentRoutes) {\n721\t      if (!EXCLUDED_LINE_VARIANTS.has(r)) {\n722\t        allLines.add(r);\n723\t      }\n724\t    }\n725\t\n726\t    stations[stationId] = {\n727\t      id: stationId,\n728\t      name,\n729\t      lat,\n730\t      lon,\n731\t      lines: Array.from(allLines).sort(),\n732\t      northStopId: northStopId || `${stationId}N`,\n733\t      southStopId: southStopId || `${stationId}S`,\n734\t      transfers: [], // Will be populated from transfers.txt\n735\t      ada: false, // Will be set from ada-stations.json\n736\t      borough: inferBorough(name, lat, lon),\n737\t    };\n738\t  }\n739\t\n740\t  // Handle orphan child stops (stops without parent_station that serve routes)\n741\t  for (const [stopId, stop] of childStops) {\n742\t    if (!stop.parent_station && stopToRoutes.has(stopId)) {\n743\t      const routes = stopToRoutes.get(stopId);\n744\t      const baseId = stopId.replace(/[NS]$/, \"\");\n745\t\n746\t      if (!stations[baseId]) {\n747\t        const direction = stopId.endsWith(\"N\") ? \"N\" : stopId.endsWith(\"S\") ? \"S\" : null;\n748\t        const lat = parseFloat(stop.stop_lat);\n749\t        const lon = parseFloat(stop.stop_lon);\n750\t\n751\t        stations[baseId] = {\n752\t          id: baseId,\n753\t          name: stop.stop_name,\n754\t          lat,\n755\t          lon,\n756\t          lines: Array.from(routes)\n757\t            .filter((r) => !EXCLUDED_LINE_VARIANTS.has(r))\n758\t            .sort(),\n759\t          northStopId: direction === \"N\" ? stopId : `${baseId}N`,\n760\t          southStopId: direction === \"S\" ? stopId : `${baseId}S`,\n761\t          transfers: [],\n762\t          ada: false,\n763\t          borough: inferBorough(stop.stop_name, lat, lon),\n764\t        };\n765\t      }\n766\t    }\n767\t  }\n768\t\n769\t  // Apply ADA overrides\n770\t  const adaIds = loadAdaOverrides(stations);\n771\t  let adaCount = 0;\n772\t  for (const id of adaIds) {\n773\t    if (stations[id]) {\n774\t      stations[id].ada = true;\n775\t      adaCount++;\n776\t    }\n777\t  }\n778\t  log(`Applied ADA status to ${adaCount} stations`);\n779\t\n780\t  log(`Processed ${Object.keys(stations).length} stations`);\n781\t  return stations;\n782\t}\n783\t\n784\t/**\n785\t * Determine if a route is express based on its route_long_name\n786\t * Express routes contain \"Express\" in the name (e.g., \"Broadway Express\", \"8th Ave Express\")\n787\t * Local routes contain \"Local\" or neither keyword\n788\t */\n789\tfunction isExpressRoute(routeLongName) {\n790\t  if (!routeLongName) return false;\n791\t  const name = routeLongName.toLowerCase();\n792\t  return name.includes(\"express\");\n793\t}\n794\t\n795\t/**\n796\t * Process routes.txt into routes.json\n797\t */\n798\tfunction processRoutes(routesData, stopTimesData, tripsData) {\n799\t  log(\"Processing routes...\");\n800\t\n801\t  // Build route_id -> stop_sequence -> stop_id\n802\t  const routeToStops = new Map();\n803\t  const tripToRoute = new Map();\n804\t  for (const trip of tripsData) {\n805\t    tripToRoute.set(trip.trip_id, trip.route_id);\n806\t  }\n807\t\n808\t  for (const st of stopTimesData) {\n809\t    const routeId = tripToRoute.get(st.trip_id);\n810\t    if (routeId) {\n811\t      if (!routeToStops.has(routeId)) {\n812\t        routeToStops.set(routeId, new Map());\n813\t      }\n814\t      const stopsMap = routeToStops.get(routeId);\n815\t      const seq = parseInt(st.stop_sequence, 10);\n816\t      if (!stopsMap.has(st.stop_id) || seq < stopsMap.get(st.stop_id)) {\n817\t        stopsMap.set(st.stop_id, seq);\n818\t      }\n819\t    }\n820\t  }\n821\t\n822\t  const routes = {};\n823\t\n824\t  for (const route of routesData) {\n825\t    const routeId = route.route_id;\n826\t\n827\t    // Map SI route to SIR\n828\t    const displayId = routeId === \"SI\" ? \"SIR\" : routeId;\n829\t\n830\t    // Skip non-subway routes (buses, ferries)\n831\t    if ([\"X\", \"SB\"].some((prefix) => routeId.startsWith(prefix))) {\n832\t      continue;\n833\t    }\n834\t\n835\t    // Use official MTA colors if available, otherwise fall back to GTFS\n836\t    const officialColor = MTA_ROUTE_COLORS[displayId];\n837\t    const color = officialColor ? officialColor.color : normalizeColor(route.route_color);\n838\t    const textColor = officialColor\n839\t      ? officialColor.textColor\n840\t      : route.route_text_color\n841\t        ? normalizeColor(route.route_text_color)\n842\t        : \"#FFFFFF\";\n843\t\n844\t    // Get ordered stops for this route\n845\t    const stopsMap = routeToStops.get(routeId) || new Map();\n846\t    const stops = Array.from(stopsMap.keys())\n847\t      .map((id) => id.replace(/[NS]$/, \"\"))\n848\t      .filter((id, i, arr) => arr.indexOf(id) === i)\n849\t      .sort((a, b) => {\n850\t        const seqA = stopsMap.get(a + \"N\") || stopsMap.get(a + \"S\") || Infinity;\n851\t        const seqB = stopsMap.get(b + \"N\") || stopsMap.get(b + \"S\") || Infinity;\n852\t        return seqA - seqB;\n853\t      });\n854\t\n855\t    routes[displayId] = {\n856\t      id: displayId,\n857\t      shortName: route.route_short_name || displayId,\n858\t      longName: route.route_long_name || \"\",\n859\t      color,\n860\t      textColor,\n861\t      feedId: FEED_MAP[displayId] || \"gtfs\",\n862\t      division: A_DIVISION_ROUTES.has(displayId) ? \"A\" : \"B\",\n863\t      stops,\n864\t      isExpress: isExpressRoute(route.route_long_name),\n865\t    };\n866\t  }\n867\t\n868\t  log(`Processed ${Object.keys(routes).length} routes`);\n869\t  return routes;\n870\t}\n871\t\n872\t/**\n873\t * Normalize hex color to uppercase with # prefix\n874\t */\n875\tfunction normalizeColor(color) {\n876\t  if (!color) return \"#808183\";\n877\t  const hex = color.replace(/^#/, \"\").toUpperCase();\n878\t  return `#${hex.padStart(6, \"0\")}`;\n879\t}\n880\t\n881\t/**\n882\t * Process transfers.txt into transfer graph\n883\t */\n884\tfunction processTransfers(transfersData, stations) {\n885\t  log(\"Processing transfers...\");\n886\t\n887\t  const transferGraph = {};\n888\t\n889\t  for (const t of transfersData) {\n890\t    const fromStop = t.from_stop_id;\n891\t    const toStop = t.to_stop_id;\n892\t\n893\t    const fromStation = fromStop.replace(/[NS]$/, \"\");\n894\t    const toStation = toStop.replace(/[NS]$/, \"\");\n895\t\n896\t    if (!stations[fromStation] || !stations[toStation]) continue;\n897\t    if (fromStation === toStation) continue;\n898\t\n899\t    if (!transferGraph[fromStation]) {\n900\t      transferGraph[fromStation] = [];\n901\t    }\n902\t\n903\t    // Use min_transfer_time, default to 180s, enforce minimum of 60s\n904\t    let walkingSeconds = parseInt(t.min_transfer_time || \"180\", 10);\n905\t    if (walkingSeconds < 60) walkingSeconds = DEFAULT_TRANSFER_SECONDS;\n906\t\n907\t    const existing = transferGraph[fromStation].find((e) => e.toStationId === toStation);\n908\t    if (existing) {\n909\t      if (walkingSeconds < existing.walkingSeconds) {\n910\t        existing.walkingSeconds = walkingSeconds;\n911\t      }\n912\t    } else {\n913\t      transferGraph[fromStation].push({\n914\t        toStationId: toStation,\n915\t        toLines: stations[toStation].lines,\n916\t        walkingSeconds,\n917\t        accessible: false, // Will be updated from equipment data\n918\t      });\n919\t    }\n920\t  }\n921\t\n922\t  // Add transfers to station objects\n923\t  for (const [stationId, transfers] of Object.entries(transferGraph)) {\n924\t    if (stations[stationId]) {\n925\t      stations[stationId].transfers = transfers;\n926\t    }\n927\t  }\n928\t\n929\t  log(`Processed ${Object.keys(transferGraph).length} transfer stations`);\n930\t  return transferGraph;\n931\t}\n932\t\n933\t/**\n934\t * Process stop_times.txt to extract inter-station travel times.\n935\t * Indexed by route_id + from_stop + to_stop for efficient lookup.\n936\t */\n937\tfunction processTravelTimes(stopTimesData, tripsData) {\n938\t  log(\"Processing travel times (this may take a moment)...\");\n939\t\n940\t  const tripToRoute = new Map();\n941\t  for (const trip of tripsData) {\n942\t    tripToRoute.set(trip.trip_id, trip.route_id);\n943\t  }\n944\t\n945\t  // Group stop_times by trip_id\n946\t  const tripStops = new Map();\n947\t  for (const st of map.set(routeId, {\n358\t      routeId,\n359\t      fetchedAt: now,\n360\t      feedAge: 0,\n361\t      trains,\n362\t    });\n363\t  }\n364\t\n365\t  return map;\n366\t}\n367\t\n368\t/**\n369\t * {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-sonnet-4-6","id":"msg_01WvZVYGft8bcZz2imAmPvT8","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Key insight from the Dockerfile: The scripts/ directory is NOT copied into the runtime image! Only these are copied:\n- `packages/server/dist/` (compiled TypeScript)\n- `packages/server/data/` (JSON data files)\n\nThe `scripts/` directory (which contains `process-gtfs.mjs`) is NOT in the runtime container.\n\nSo running `node scripts/process-gtfs.mjs` from within the server process won't work in production - the script file won't be there.\n\nThis changes the approach significantly. Options:\n1. **Add scripts/ to the Dockerfile** - copy it in alongside the built output\n\n\n2. **Convert process-gtfs.mjs to TypeScript and import it directly** - compile it as part of the server build\n3. **Argo Workflows template** - run the script externally, commit the updated JSON to the repo, trigger a rebuild\n\nOption 1 is simple but slightly wasteful. Option 2 requires significant refactoring. Option 3 is cleanest for this use case, though I need to reconcile it with the constraint against K8s Jobs/CronJobs — Argo Workflows might actually be the right fit here since it's a separate orchestration layer rather than native K8s scheduling.\n\nActually, let me reconsider Option 1: I could copy the scripts into the runtime image and implement an in-server scheduler using setInterval, keeping everything self-contained within the container and the data files writable at runtime.\n\nBut there's a critical flaw—in Kubernetes, when the pod restarts (whether from a deployment update, memory pressure, or any other reason), the container filesystem resets to what's baked into the Docker image, so any file updates written during runtime get lost unless they're persisted to a PersistentVolume. This means the weekly GTFS refresh would update the files temporarily, but the next pod restart would reload the stale data from the image.\n\nThe cleanest solution is to have the server itself run the refresh scheduler, and after the script successfully updates the files, trigger a graceful process exit so Kubernetes automatically restarts the pod and it loads the fresh data into memory. This way, the refresh cycle is self-contained: update files → exit cleanly → pod restarts → loads new data.\n\nBut wait—if the data directory isn't persisted across container restarts, the updated files will be lost when Kubernetes spins up a fresh container from the image. So this only works if the data lives on a PersistentVolume. Otherwise, the real solution is to use Argo Workflows to run the GTFS processing, commit the updated JSON back to the git repo, and let the existing CI pipeline rebuild and redeploy the Docker image with the fresh data baked in.\n\nHowever, the constraints say no K8s Jobs or CronJobs—I need to use long-running Deployments with internal scheduling instead. So the approach is to add a setInterval in the server startup that triggers the GTFS download and parse logic weekly, keeping everything within the running application itself. I can implement both approaches—an Argo WorkflowTemplate for weekly GTFS refreshes that commits back to the repo and triggers new builds, plus an in-server scheduler as a fallback. The Argo approach is cleaner since it keeps the server decoupled from git operations and ensures fresh data in every image, while the in-server option would require PersistentVolumes or restart logic to persist updates across pod cycles.\n\nNow I'm realizing the Argo template would need to live in the declarative-config repo rather than here, which creates a coordination issue between the two repositories.\n\nFor this bead, I should focus on what can actually be implemented in the mta-my-way repo itself: setting up an in-server scheduler, adding the scripts to the Dockerfile so they're available in the container, and documenting that data persistence across restarts requires either manual image rebuilds or a separate Argo workflow setup in declarative-config.\n\nLet me look back at what the task is actually asking for—it mentions there's no automation at all currently, so I need to clarify what's feasible to implement here versus what would require changes elsewhere. JSON files in packages/server/data/ are only updated when a developer runs the script manually. The task is explicitly about automation, so I need to move away from that manual approach.\n\nIf I use setInterval within the server, the updates would persist as long as the pod stays running, which is reasonable for a stable production service that doesn't restart frequently. The data directory is already writable in the Dockerfile, so that's not a blocker—but the scripts directory isn't included in the container image, which is the real problem.\n\nMy plan is to copy the scripts into the Dockerfile, create a scheduler module that runs the GTFS refresh weekly, wire it into the main server, and also set up an Argo CronWorkflow for declarative scheduling. I'm still deciding whether the Argo template belongs in this repo or in the separate declarative-config repository where other templates live.\n\nActually, I'll keep it simple and focus on the in-server scheduler approach—that's what the documentation recommends anyway. I'll copy the scripts into the image, create the scheduler, and wire it up. This gives me minimal viable automation: the data refreshes weekly in long-running containers, and if a pod restarts, it uses the latest data baked into the image until the next scheduled refresh kicks in.\n\nFor the implementation, I need to update the Dockerfile to include the scripts, create a refresh module, and hook it into the server startup. The tricky part is getting the paths right—the server runs from `/app/packages/server/dist/index.js`, so I need to calculate the script path relative to that location and set the working directory correctly when spawning the process.\n\nSetting up the scheduler module... I'm weighing whether to check data freshness on startup or stick with a simple weekly schedule—the latter seems cleaner since the developer will have recently refreshed everything before deploying. I'll go with a 7-day interval starting 7 days after startup, log when the next run happens, and keep the implementation straightforward.\n\nWriting the scheduler implementation... Writing the refresh handler... Writing the scheduler logic... I'm verifying the logger signature matches across the codebase—it takes a message string and optional context object for `info`, and message plus an Error object and optional context for `error`. My implementation looks aligned with that pattern. For the `collectOutput` function, I'll skip the verbose flag to avoid log spam and instead just capture stderr for any errors, logging the start and end with the exit code. For the production approach, the scheduler will run weekly to download and parse new GTFS files, writing the updated JSON to `/app/packages/server/data/`, though the in-memory data would need a restart to pick up the changes.\n\nBut I'm realizing there's a fundamental issue here—when Kubernetes restarts a pod, it recreates the container from the image, so any runtime file updates to the data directory are lost since it's baked into the image, not on a PersistentVolume. For this to actually work, I'd need either a mounted PersistentVolume for the data directory or implement hot-reloading of the data after refresh. I should check the Kubernetes deployment config to see if there's already a PV set up, but since I don't have access to that repo, I need to think about what the task is really asking for—automating GTFS data updates so they don't require manual intervention.\n\nThe in-server scheduler approach with the current setup is essentially writing to ephemeral disk and refreshing stale in-memory data, which doesn't serve a production purpose unless I add logic to actually reload the in-memory data after the files are updated.\n\nLooking at how the data structures are initialized and passed to multiple subsystems, a hot-reload would be complex—I'd need to re-initialize the app itself and all the dependent services that reference these data structures, which isn't straightforward in a running server.\n\nThe simpler approach would be to just exit the process after writing the new GTFS files and let Kubernetes restart the pod, but that only works if the data directory is on a PersistentVolume; otherwise the new pod reads from the original image and loses the updates.\n\nSo I'm back to weighing the real options: either use Argo CronWorkflow with git commits for a clean declarative setup, or accept the limitations of the in-server scheduler approach.\n\nLooking at the task description again, it's clear the intended solution is the Argo approach—a weekly CronWorkflow that processes the GTFS data, commits the updated JSON back to the repo, triggers a new Docker build via GitHub webhook, and then ArgoCD redeploys with the fresh data baked into the image.\n\nThe challenge is that implementing this properly requires changes to the declarative-config repo, which is outside the scope of this work.
